<Author>FREQUENTTRIPPERPerth
<Content>Not For the Feint Hearted I booked and had confirmed an 'Ocean View' room. When I was shown to the room on arrival it had a view of the balconies of the adjoining building and a small amount of garden. When I explained that this is not what I had paid for the room was changed - again ithis room did not have a direct ocean view but was more pleasant.The hotel is not for the elderly or the feint hearted. The restaurants, pool and bars are reached by means of stairs which are not well illuminated at night and there are no hand rails. Everything is spread out and it can take up to ten minutes walking to get to a location and retutn to the room.Another problem is the remote locaton of the complex. This tends to make the visitor a captive to the dining and beverage facilties at the hotel which are very expensive by Bali standards.Boquets must be awared to good service and smiling staff.

<Author>jbebb
<Content>Disappointment at the Ritz We were really excited to visit the Ritz ... it was the last night of our honeymoon in Bali and my husband wanted it to be really special. He booked a King Deluxe Room and explained in the booking it was our honeymoon. All the other hotels has gone above and beyond for us thus far and we were looking forward to staying at this hotel -- we got married in Bali too and had almost decided to have our wedding at the Ritz -- luckily we didn't!We were greeted warmly as we got out of the cab, but the staff just pointed ahead of us indicating we should just take ourselves to the lobby to check in. We had no idea where we were supposed to go. Once in the lobby we stood around for a while waiting for someone to notice us, eventually they did but kept us waiting almost 20 minutes before we were given our keys... which I had to go and ask for twice! They had plenty of notice we were coming down the incredibly long driveway (security checked our booking at the exterior gate and we assumed they call ahead) so there's no excuse to not have one point of contact greet you and take you to the lobby to check in. That one person should see to everything instead of us bumbling around with multiple people who all seemed like they had no idea at what stage our check in was at!We were shown to our room but once inside were surprised to see 2 separate single beds... one with a few rose petals sprinkled on them. Nice touch but did someone actually think that a honeymoon couple would be cool with 2 separate single beds?! The staff was apologetic but was quick to add there was nothing she could do but arrange for housekeeping to push the 2 beds together. My husband had had about enough of the place by then as he'd noticed black mould growing all through the bathroom shower and door frames. I rang the duty manager to complain and eventually they found another room for us (despite the fact that earlier it was impossible). Over an hour passed and we quickly got to the other room, changed into our bathers to make it down to the pool just in time for the sunset... we were doubly surprised that the Ritz pools close AT SUNSET!!! They are situated on a cliff overlooking the ocean on a sunset beach and they close the pools so incredibly early. We could hardly believe it. Was this normal? The pool staff indicated it was time to go by taking our pool chair cushions out from under our things while we were in the pool. Not a great start! We were only there one night before our flight out of Bali and it was almost getting laughable...I must say, the food however at the Italian restaurant was lovely. We enjoyed our meal a lot! In some parts of the hotel it was looking a little tired... I think it's time for some upgrades to some parts of the hotel grounds. Perhaps the fact we were only there one night was enough excuse for the Ritz to not expend any service energy on us. Despite the fact we were upgraded to a nicer room after I expressed my concerns about the initial room, I would hesitate before going back there again. It's like the hotel is too big for it's own good!  
<Date>Nov 17, 2008

<Author>Ppong
<Content>Unforgettable stay Both partner and I are members of the Marriott Vacation Club and so for our 1st trip booked via them, we decided to try staying at the Ritz in Bali as our experience in staying at the Club Suite in Singapore was fantastic. Luxurious accomodations and excellent service and also not forgetting the Bvlgari toiletries which we thoroughly enjoyed. This is our 2nd trip to Bali - formerly we stayed at Candidasa (Candi Beach Cottage) in Dec 2007. It was very tranquil and part of reason we visited Bali again was that we felt that we didn't really do Bali justice as Candidasa is rather remote and the beach there wasn't great.This trip we were there from 4 - 10 Sept 2008. First 2 days we stayed at Nusa Dua - 1st night at Kind Villa Bintang (very pleasant stay) and the 2nd night at Oasis Beach Resort (poor service - don't stay there). So anyway, we rented a vehicle and we made our way to Ritz Carlton with a map in hand and lots of help from the locals. It was a very interesting uphill drive and when we reached the security check-point, we still had to drive through a very long driveway to reach the hotel lobby. The grounds were immensely huge and we still thought Four Seasons was large when we passed by on the way in.Anyway, check-in was great, we had our welcome drink in the lobby while taking in the view. And a fantastic surprise was when they told us they had upgraded us to a garden terrace suite. (we were kinda hoping for an upgrade as we read many reviews that a free upgrade was possible.) We had a guide who led us to our room and our jaws dropped when we saw the expanse of the suite... large living area with a large LCD tv, patio, large four poster bed equipped with another tv and the bathroom - double vanity with separate bath tub (with a petal bath ready for us) and shower. Oh right, there's another guest bathroom and shower at the entrance of the suite. As we booked for a standard room, this was a real treat for us.Once we settled down, we went for the resort tour on a buggy and we mentally noted what our itinery would be for the next few days. There were 2 beaches, Kubu beach and Kisik beach. Both of which are accessible via a long flight of stone steps. 3 pools, main infinity pool, aquarium pool and the ocean-view infinity pool. We visited the Kubu beach most often as there were less people there and somehow the sun was out more often there. We also arranged for the mediterranean lunchbox for 2 while we were there. Can't remember the price - approx. US30-40 per person. The spread was surprisingly extensive. Kubu beach is not really for swimming though, the waves were rather strong and I got tossed around the shore when the waves came in. Got some abrasions on my thighs for that but it was really good fun. The view is fantastic at the top and we descended the 160+ steps 3 times during our stay in good humor with sore thighs thereafter.The main pool bar was great as well - more accessible than the beaches, do try the wood-fire pizzas at the pool bar, really delicious and their presentation of cocktails was really lovely. We did try the Aquatonic pool at the Spa one evening. Was really interesting with various stations with jets placed for a different purpose - an invigorating exercise. The spa grounds was very pretty and the service was tip-tops. But don't wear white swim-wear as my new white bikini ended up with permanent yellow stains due to the sea-water content.Dining-wise, breakfast at Sami Sami was great. Great views and great food - well presented which was no surprise. We had breakfast at Padi one of the mornings - buffet style. Very extensive spread - egg,waffles and pancakes station. The bakery section was extensive too with a great selection of jams and spreads. You get chinese and japanese selections as well on top of the usual. However, if you don't have a great appetite like us, it is more worth it to order ala-carte at Sami Sami. We learnt that if you order a main dish - the juices, tea and bakery items profferred were at no additional cost. This is what I call value-added. We hardly had lunch as our breakfast was usually late so afternoon snacks at the pool sufficed till dinner. We ate out at Jimbaran bay (Sharkey) and Kedoganan Bay (Fortuin Cafe). Prices there are very competitive and cheap - US45 for the both of us. Grilled whole snapper, clams, lobster, calamari. The service staff are very willing to serve.We did visit 2 other spas in the Jimbaran area - Aroma Talk (we tried the hot stone treatment packages and shirodhara.) and Sekar Jagat (Shiatsu and Aloe Wrap for our sunburnt skin). Both highly recommended. Aroma Talk has really nice gardens and villas for treatments. Sekar Jagat is more traditional - authentic balinese surroundings. On the whole, Ritz is pretty self-contained. If you prefer to get out of the resort grounds, then having a vehicle would make sense. (Anyway, most restaurants around Jimbaran offers free transport back and fro at no cost.) Then again, the resort grounds are so pretty and the food at the numerous restaurants is good enough to keep you at the resort. Of course, you do pay a price for that. A coconut drink cost about USD10 which you can get for US2 elsewhere. I must say that the service level is fantastic, the staff are very helpful and attentive and honest as well. We were hardly in the suite most of the time and nothing was missing.If you ask if I would return, yes for sure! We didn't even want to leave. Checking out was not without regrets. We had a really great time. Everyday was paradise for both of us.  
<Date>Oct 28, 2008

<Author>lauralynn131313
<Content>Stay somewhere else next time My husband and I went to the Ritz for a wedding. We were really looking forward to staying at the Ritz again, because we got married at the Ritz in Laguna Beach/Dana Point in California. We arrived at the Ritz 8 days into our trip to Bali, after staying at the Nusa Dua Hotel and Spa and a beautiful local hotel in Ubud. In both places we were upgraded to suites and or villas, full of Balinese culture, charm and elegance and lots of amenities. Upon arriving at the Ritz we were very disappointed with our ocean view room, that looked like any other room in any other Ritz hotel around the world. In other words it lacked much Balinese culture and style. The amenities that were included with our other hotels that we stayed at before the Ritz, far outweighed what was included at the Ritz and at a more affordable price. Paying $10 an hour for internet service is ridiculous, when we got it for free at all other hotels, drinks super expensive with little alcohol, food ok, and the grounds lacked the true Balinese culture and feel. Additionally the room didn't have any drawer space which I thought was odd at a 5 star hotel. The ocean front infinity pool was the highlight of the trip along with a great spa treatment. But overall I thought the value was not there for the money. When we return to Bali we won't be going to the Ritz. The competition is too good with other hotels that offer more value for your money.

<Author>cttraveler07
<Content>loved the resort, but very disappointed with Dava and customer service We stayed at the Ritz Carlton Jimbaran Bay for 2 nights as part of our honeymoon. As soon as we arrived, we were very impressed with the resort. The grounds were very nice and the pools were gorgeous, especially the infinity oceanfront pool. We upgraded to a 1 bedroom suite and it was very spacious.However, our vacation was basically ruined because on the 2nd night, we had the tasting menu at Dava Restaurant, which is supposedly their best restaurant. Both of us came down with horrible food poisoning that night. The next day we needed to check out, and I told customer service that we got sick from the Dava dinner. They did not take my complaint very seriously. All they offered was some carbonated drinks and a free cab ride to the airport. I could not believe that was the treatment we got at a 5 star hotel, especially since they could see that we were still very ill. So I refused to settle the bill until the best they would give me was 30% back from the dinner check. After I returned home, I wrote a complaint letter, which was addressed by a manager at the Bali resort, as well as corporate customer service. But I am still disappointed that I had to go through so much effort just to get some sort of reimbursement for the hotel making us horribly sick. I will also add that one afternoon while taking a shower, the cold water cut out and we were suddenly scalded by hot water. They did fix this, but I do not understand how this happened either. The food at the restaurants is mediocre at best. We had our first dinner at Padi Restaurant, and the thai food was no better than an average thai restuarant. The food at Dava was ironically not very good at all. The breakfast buffet has a pretty extensive selection and many fresh fruits. We liked the Martini Club, the drinks were interesting and the bar was beautifully designed.As I said before, the pools are wonderful, and definitely the highlight of our stay there. The private beach that you take a shuttle to is also very nice, but you must climb down many flights of stairs to reach the beach, and it is quite a workout to walk back up the stairs to leave. At least there is a person waiting at the top of the steps to give you a bottle of water and call the shuttle for you.I agree with a previous post that the charge for internet is pretty steep. Overall, a decent stay if we had not gotten food poisoned, but not the 5 star experience I expected.

<Content>Good resort hotel We liked the Ritz in Bali. A few of the good things we liked were the staff was very nice. <Author>AmandaChitown
<Content>Amazing hotel Just returned from spending the last 3 nights of a 7 night stay in Bali and cannot say enough great things about it. We were luckily enough to get upgraded to an ocean view cliff villa which was several levels higher than the deluxe ocean view room we booked. It was 4,000 SF with a gorgeous view of the Indian Ocean, a massive living room, bedroom and bathroom. Our own private pool and resting area were out back. The bathroom had a separate soaking tub, walk in shower with rainfall showerhead with the same amazing view of the ocean. The hotel itself is isolated up on the cliffs of Jimbaran, and the grounds are massive with several different bars and restaurants to explore. If you are going to Bali to explore different parts of the island and see the sights, stay somewhere else for that part because once you get to the Ritz you'll never want to leave! It worked out well for us because we stayed in Sanur for the first part of our holiday and then treated ourselves to the Ritz at the end. We did eat any dinners at the Ritz as we took taxis into Kuta or Seminyak for meals and bars. As you would expect at any Ritz, the service was unbelievable. You have your own butlers that will take care of anything you need at any time of the day. They remember what you ordered for lunch and will serve it to you while in your private pool. We had a breakfast buffet included everyday which had a great selection of all types of breakfast foods and also had drinks at the Martini Bar one night before going out. They know you by name after the first day and buggies are available to take you from your villa to the various pools and restaurants (the grounds are too big and hilly to walk on your own, depending on where your room is). We felt the best pool area and hot tub was the Villa Pool. We had no problems getting a taxi or driver when needed. They were very accomodating holding our bags and giving us the Spa facilities to use while after we checked out and while waiting for our nightime flight. We were lucky enough to get the gorgeous villa at a significantly lower rate, so if you're able to save up enough to afford it, or you can afford it, I would highly recommend it! I'm not a frequent Ritz Carlton guest, so it was quite the treat for me.

<Author>Kris71
<Content>Needs to be much more! We travel to Bali quite often and normally stay in the Hyatt in Nusa Dua or the Intercontinental but decided that we would give the Ritz Carlton a try as we had read a lot of good reviews here!Well i have to say we will not be going back!!!For what it costs it is certainly not value for money!We booked a club room but were advised on check in that our 10 year old daughter would not be allowed into the club lounge! so there was a total waste of money! we were informed that we could take breakfast in Padi (where everyone else has breakfast!) The only difference i can see between the club room and the standard is that with the club you get a designated floor to check in and the lounge, which we could not use!The rooms are no larger than any other rooms in Bali! though the standard rooms in Hyatt are much bigger and much better value for money!The food and drinks poolside are astronomical but i have to say that the poolside staff are very good and attentive most of the time, though Ritz Carlton need more poolside loungers!!! on 2 occasions we could not get a bed... now if i am paying $580 a night i expect to be able to sit by the pool!The hairdryer in our club room overheated every 15 seconds of constant use and then i had to wait 10 minutes for it to cool down, i requested a new one from housekeeping and they sent me a 350 watt hairdryer (the normal wattage of a hairdryer is 1200) so it was like someone breathing on my hair, no power no heat, i requested another yet this never materialised... these are essential items in hotels rooms!! the amenities were good though the shampoo and conditioner are awful and leave hair feeling dry. The whole resorts white towels and facecloths need to be thrown away as my whole 4 night stay i only got 1 white fluffy towel, the rest were that lovely washed out grey and hard type that you expect when paying $50 dollar a nightThe Martini lounge was amazing and the staff were what you expect in a 5* hotel..... Padi Restaurant is good but again i have eaten better Thai food!We went to Sami Sami the italian on our 1st night and that was ok! though the bottle of wine we ordered cost an amazing 拢110 for a 拢20 maximum bottle elsewhere!If your looking for a real Bali feel then this is not the place, you could be anywhere....... We also booked a hotel car to take us to Ku De Ta one evening to see the sunset and have dinner, we had to wait over 15 minutes b4 our car arrived and subsequently only got to see the very end of the sunset.. if i book a car for a time then i expect it to be ready..This to say the least is not my idea of a great resort, i have stayed in the Ritz in Hong Kong, Dubai (which is amazing and should be tried) and Kuala Lumpur but to be honest i will not be rushing back to stay in the Ritz Bali anytime soon!I think they need to take a very long hard look at what they offer and make some severe changes!

<Author>charkey
<Content>Divine... Absolutely stunning resort...grounds and rooms are immaculate, service is second to none, I have never experienced such excellent service, felt like royalty, all the staff so lovely and polite, they remembered our names after serving us only once. Food was spectacular in all of the restaurants. Ritz Kids Club truly fantastic...beautiful staff who obviously adore children run it and keep the little ones entertained (our children PLEADED with us to go there every day, something we didn't do as we had day trips planned, but it's good to know that they enjoyed it so much) and an excellent nanny service should you wish to go out at night without the kids. Whilst the room rate is extremely reasonable considering the level of luxury and service one receives when staying there, beware of everything else at the resort, such as the restaurants, shops and spa......they certainly don't miss you there as far as charging top dollar...but I guess you pay for the convenience because you don't have to worry about getting in a car or taxi for a half-hour journey into Seminyak, Kuta, Sanur etc just for cheaper massages, meals and shopping (and I might argue that at the Ritz-Carlton it's all top notch, unlike some of the services, food and shopping you might get in those other places.)

<Author>Tokyodude
<Content>Nice hotel, but a bit overpriced I booked an Oceanfront villa through Amex since they said that if an upgrade was available, I would be upgraded. When I got there, the villa front desk (it's different from the regular front desk) told us that the upgrades don't apply to villas. So we ended up staying at the villa we booked. The villas is in front of the ocean, but so is a bunch of other villas, which means that if you walk forward to see the ocean, you can see into the other people's villas and vice versa (not much privacy here). The so called plunge pool is not really a pool but a size of a jacuzzi which was a dissapointment. The inside of the room itself was really clean and nice, but not too big compared to other villas of Bali (had a bedroom, living room, walk-in closet, nice 2 person bathtub, shower etc). When we checked in, the butler drove us to the villa and told us to simply dial 0 to reach him. When I tried that, I always got the hotel operator and nobody could really tell me how to get in touch with my so called private butler (all they said was they would relay any request I had). Also, I was a bit surprised that many of the staff didn't speak English that well (if you asked for anything out of the oridinary, I had a hard time making them understand). As far as the grounds of the Ritz, there are lots of resuturants, pools, a private beach (nice, but lots of rocks so watch out) and activities to keep you busy. But the impression I got, was that in the main areas outsides of the villa area, it was a bit noisy and too many people to call it a relaxed atmosphere. Also the resturant prices are a bit pricy, but since the Ritz is away from everything else, you are baisically forced to eat all your meals here (for example a drink I had at the pool cost about $10). Also the grounds are nice for sure, but it doesn't have a Bali look to it. I felt like I could've been in Hawaii or Thailand and it would still look the same.Besides the resturants, some other prices that kind of surprised me:1) No free internet. They have wireless in the villas, but they charge about $10 / hour for it....ridiculous2) When I asked for transportation back to the airport, they told me it would cost me $30. I called a cab and ended up paying $7.I would've expected some these costs, but when you are already paying about $700 / night for the villas, can't they give me free interenet and a ride back to the airport as a service?Most of the staff was nice, but compared to some other Bali places, I felt that the friendly spirit that I love Bali for wasn't there.Overall I would have to say that for the price I was paying, I would've expected more and I wouldn't stay here again.

<Author>LiQ-American
<Content>Overall, Great!! " Without a doubt, this was a very enjoyable stay. We booked it for 4 nights for the end of June and when we arrived we were pleasantly surprised at how many Javanese families were staying at the hotel. As it turned out, the vacation period had just begun for Indonesia. The feel of the hotel became lively and always interesting. Some families enjoyed teaching us some Indonesian phrases. My wife and I truly enjoyed the private beach and the salt water swimming pool, (no kids under 12 years old allowed without an adult). It was well worth the 148 steep steps down the side of a hill to get there. Unfortunately, we were unable to go swimming in the waves, for red flags were posted each day we were there. However, this was not a problem for they have a salt water swimming pool that gives you the illusion of being eye level to the ocean, although you're about 20 meters above it. Serinity at its finest. There were a couple of negative situations that should be mentioned, but didn't ruin our overall stay here. The breakfast wasn't very good and limited in selection. We had to compete with the fruit flies, for food for the buffet area was out in the open and not in an enclosed area. There were also birds flying around in the bread area. We didn't stay in the Club , so it may be better off on that end. Also, on our first morning of our stay, we arrived at the breakfast buffet area at 7:30am and were told that they didn't have any available seats for two and we would have to wait for 10 minutes. This was fine, for it gave me ample time to go to the front desk and complain personally to the manager that my newspaper hadn't been sent to my room , as had been requested. I was also able to tell him my first impressions of the breakfast buffet area. The manager was Goood. He had a way of defusing me and letting the steam out of my kettle to the point that I had forgotten why I went to see him. Needless to say, the missing newspaper situation never happened again, and I had a better attitude when seated for our buffet breakfast. The other situation that should be mentioned was their overpriced restaurants, and the low exchange rates offered by the hotel for USD to INR. In the evenings, my wife and I would take a taxi to the Intercontinental Hotel down the road, to exchange money (Close to/the same as posted by Bloomberg), and also to enjoy their reasonably priced sunset dinners. This other hotel also had a regular shuttle to the DFS in Kuta.  My wife told me I shouldn't concern myself with the the price of things at the Ritz, for it IS The Ritz. However, in my mind, you should get what you pay for and nothing less than that. Other than these two situations, our overall stay at this hotel was wonderful. The great people that worked there, and the diversity and friendliness of all the people we encountered on our 5 day stay at this hotel will always be positively remembered.  On another note, a few European guests took us in as students in the sport of soccer, or football as the rest of the world calls it. We spent a very pleasant evening watching the Euro-Cup with these lads and their families. They even allowed me to wear my New England Patriots football shirt. I think they appreciated the effort from this American soccer student.

<Author>traveler30
<Content>Mixed Feelings I can't say too much negative about this hotel, but I really can't say a lot positive either.It's a Ritz, which means a very nice room and very nice grounds. It is disappointing that the hotel doesn't have its own beach, but does offer a shuttle to a beach about a mile away. On an island with lots of beach resorts, I consider this a major drawback.The staff was very nice and very helpful. I booked a club rooom, so it was nice to have access to the club lounge. I was a little surprised that the head of concierge did not send over some flowers or something after I mentioned we were on our honeymoon. I also struggle with the reality that I ended up paying nearly $8 for an order of french fries on an island where you can have an entire seafood dinner for that amount. I certainly didn't expect the Ritz to be inexpensive, but the prices being so out of line with the local economy when I know the staff are not the ones getting the extra dollars always bugs me. I have to admit favoring some of the local resorts that are not dramatically cheaper, but just seem more fair.I won't suggest passig on the Ritz, but I would suggest at least trying other properties also if you do choose it.

<Content>Superlative Friends and I booked Club Rooms. In retrospect, that was a truly brilliant decision. <Author>BerkeleyTravelAddict
<Content>Don't believe the negative reviews I have stayed at the Ritz Carlton Bali 5 years in a row and my stay in March, 2008 was by far the best. We stayed in a Club room that was beautiful. The remodeled Club lounge was stunning. The food presentations were inspired and delicious. The newest feature of the hotel is an amazing infinity edge pool (the 3rd pool on the property) perched between the ocean's edge and the base of a cliff. The experience of feeling the spray from the crashing surf while floating in this incredible new pool was unreal. The Ritz has stepped things up from my past visits and I would certainly return. Other than one or two tour groups gathering in the morning in the main lobby, there were no large crowds as reported by other reviewers. Mid day I counted 8 people at the main pool and 3 others at the new ocean side pool. The staff was incredibly attentive and polite. I strongly recommend booking a club room which includes full breakfast, a light lunch service, afternoon tea, heavy appetizers, desserts and beverages (including alcohol served all day). This hotel is world class.

<Author>jcjchung
<Content>One of the BEST!!! I spend over 3 months of the year in hotels and this is one of the best I have ever stayed in. We checked in at 10pm were upgraded to a Club room. The oceanview club room was amazing with a large balcony, 2 bathrooms both with showers and a seperate lounge area.The Ritz property is amazing. 3 pools and a private beach. I particularly liked the salt water pool on the cliff. The pool side service was fantastic. You must try and watermelon juice that is served in a full sized watermelon.The service was excellent and staff were extremely well trained. There is so much attention to detail at this hotel and was beyond my expectations. Firstly, at the pool, I was provided with a selection of ipods, each ipod has a different music genre. Secondly after walking up the nasty stairs from the cliff pool, we were provided with cold scented towels to cool off. I did not eat at any of the restaurants but we had (2 of us) room service twice and pool side lunch and the total was approx US$100 which I thought was very reasonably priced. All the food we ate at the Ritz were really tasty. The Nasi Goreng was the best I have ever tasted. The hotel is popular with asian luxury tourist and NOT groups. I spoke to one of the people at the hotel. It is approx 35% Japanese, 15% Koreans, 15% Russians, 10% Taiwanese, 10% Hong Kong, 15% mixed Australia/ French/ German/ Singapore. You will find that most of the staff speaks Japanese. I was told none are groups except for the Taiwanese.Being a popular destination for non sun bathing asian tourist is quite an advantage as it leaves plenty of deck chairs available for sunbathers. The diversity of different nationality also means breakfast was a smogasbord of western, japanese, chinese, scandinavian breakfast available. Yummy!There were 2 locations for breakfast. One was the buffet and the other was a-la-cart. I personally prefered the a-la-cart next to the pool.On the downside, i did notice the thin walls. I could hear next door's tv and some coughing from my lounge room. I also thought the private beach was overrated and the internet was disgustingly expensive US$7 for 30mins.Overall, I thought this hotel is well maintained, well runned and its people are well trained!!!

<Author>ssmk
<Content>Too many loud people This was my second time staying at this hotel. My first was two years ago as a newlywed. This time, I came with my husband, one year old son and another couple. Last time I was very impressed. We stayed on the club level and the hotel did not seem crowded. I chose the Ritz again because we wanted a beach accessible resort style hotel where everyone would always have something to do. I do not like the feel of Nusa Dua (too manicured and flat.) I have never stayed at another Balinese beach, but liked the waves of Jimbaran. We stayed for 3 days exclusively within the hotel and then went to Ubud (Komaneka) for 5 days. This time I have mixed feeling about our stay.The setting (on the cliff), the beach , saltwater pool, Kisik, Dava martini lounge for drinks, and parts of the landscape are incredible. Unfortunately, I often felt that there were several bus loads of tourists with a package deal who were dropped off daily. Also, the food and the level of service were inconsistence.  We chose an ocean view room. We would have booked the club level, but were unable to, because children are not allowed. Eating at the Padi restaurant breakfast buffet was a horrible experience. It was too crowded, and I encountered a very rude guest. Actually, I would avoid this restaurant all together. We also went there for dinner and the Thai food and service was not very good. Otherwise we had a sunset dinner at Kisik, pool-side meals, and breakfast at Dava which were all good. During the day, we went to the Kuba beach which was practically empty. Kuba beach is one of my favorite features of the RItz. We also enjoyed the main pool and the saltwater pool. My son had fun in the play room. They should have more outside toys/structures with shade. The children's pool should be updated. Ths spa is nice. I did not have the best massage or body scrub, but it was good. There is a variety of treatments. Last time our treatments were during the day. This time they were at night. I preferred this. When I left my massage room, the enviornment outside was so quiet and peaceful. All the staff was very nice. They did not seem fake. I think the Balinese in general are very warm and friendly. The people and their strong traditions and beliefs are why my husband keep coming back to Bali. I asked a waiter about the 10 % service charge on everything. All the staff split this. This resort is not that child friendly. I am referring to all the stairs. We brought our stroller everywhere because it serves as a high chair too. (Though, there were sturdy/belted high chairs at the restaurants.) This was sometimes very difficult. I saw one wheelchair, but am not sure how they managed to get everywhere except for the golf carts. I did feel comfortable with my son being loud and active, because there was so much going on. And, there was plenty of grass for him to run on. When we stayed in Ubud (Komaneka) I often felt that he was making too much noise. Overall, my friends and I enjoyed our stay. It was there first time, and they though the place was beautiful. This is a good place if you are with big group with varied interests. If you stay here, stay at the club level and avoid the high season. I have a feeling that the rooms are being sold with a package deal in some countries, so this may never happen. The grounds and pool are very beautiful. I am glad that we did stay here at least once. If you don't stay here, come to Dava for a martini. Next time, I will try a different hotel .

<Author>MaisieNewYork
<Content>A Lesson in Compromise I stayed in the Ritz Carlton based on exceptionally low rates on the company's website and glowing online reviews. Although I'm hardly a devotee of the Ritz Carlton brand, it was at the end of a six week trip through Southeast Asia--and after staying at the legendary hotels in other cities, I thought perhaps I could forgo one top hotel on my trip and still be reasonably comfortable and contented with my choice. I was wrong. The Ritz was teeming with tourist groups and families who had no doubt been lured (like me!) by the rate and the raves about the property's amenities and signature saltwater Thalasso spa. Although the grounds were lush with flora and beautifully landscaped gardens, the din of the lobby and crowded pool area was not remotely resort-like or relaxing. It felt more like a convention taken over by the spouses and offspring of the conventioneers.Once shown to my room, I was immediately taken by the cheap quality of the materials used to furnish it--quintessential Ritz style chintz and marble on a poor man's budget. What's more, the walls were paper thin. I could hear the couple next door talking as if they were standing behind my headboard.The next morning, I was awakened at 7:30AM by loud chatter and laughter outside my window. When I drew the curtains back, I was astonished to see three employees gardening five feet outside of my room, socializing as loudly as if it were the middle of the day! I went to the breakfast buffet--which was jam packed with families and children--and immediately felt queasy after drinking the orange juice and tasting my cold scrambled eggs. My spirits were further soured by unsightly unbussed cups and saucers at the only free table I could find. I sustained a mild case of food poisoning from breakfast, and spent the early part of the afternoon resting in the room and wearing earplugs to drown out the noise of the gardeners on one side of my room, and hotel guests passing by my door on the other.The poor customer service didn't stop with dirty dishes and rude gardeners. On several occasions I asked the concierge to help me book a tour or deliver a newspaper to my room. In the Hong Kong Peninsula or the Raffles in Singapore I would have received cordial phone messages and faxes confirming my requests. At the Ritz Carlton, they blew them off. I never received a copy of the daily morning paper I saw at other people's doors. Finally, on my second evening, twisting my body like a contortionist while training my camera on the setting sun, trying to achieve the illusion of a tranquil sunset (hundreds of people around me, I'm not exaggerating, were marring the frame and taking pictures of that sun!), I had had it. I went up to my room and called the Four Seasons in Sayan, Ubud. I explained the noise/crowd issue to the manager, who was sympathetic to my plight and told me he had heard the complaints many times before. He offered me a peaceful villa with a plunge pool and breakfast. I checked out of that noisy, crowded, poor imitation of a five star luxury hotel and never looked back.

<Author>TheTraveller65
<Content>Disappointed! My favourite part of about this hotel is the view from the lobby looking down to the ocean and the pool and restaurant down by the ocean. The staff are also very nice and professional as found in all RC. But what i did not like about the hotel was it was so big and spreadout! It really has everything you could possibly want, spa, gym, tennis, endless choices of restaurants and bars.... but with so many great restaurants in Bali it is a shame to stay at the hotel the entire time. The restaurants and bars were empty which guess proves my point. We were there in Jan and it seemed like the only people who were there were either Japanese or Russians. Stayed 1 night and checked out 5 days early. I prefer smaller more intimate places. If you have children or like to stay in a big resort then this is your cup of tea. But if you go to Bali for R  R then I would look elsewhere.

<Author>Mr_Ushooz
<Content>Stay away! One of the most OVER RATED resorts in the world I travel a lot (have been to over 40 countries), and have stayed in many resorts, from 1 star to 5 star.I am baffled at some of the comments about the Ritz Bali on Trip advisor. Maybe the other people writing reviews have not traveled much, only going to fancy resorts for a honeymoon or anniversary.I must say the Ritz Carlton in Bali is the most over rated hotel/resort I have ever stayed in.I stayed in an Ocean front Villa for three days in January 2008. The Villa was nice, but at around $700 per night, it had better be.However, the service and attention to detail at this resort is horrendous. The staff seems fake, almost to the point you get the feeling they resent you (the average wage for a worker in Bali is $100 per MONTH).Service at the restaurants is poor. After being seated, you often wait more than 10 minutes just to asked if you want something to drink. The Spa claims to be one of the best in the world. I find that to be flat out lie. Much better spas exist outside the hotel. The grounds are big and spacious, but nothing special. In fact, there are often bags of trash left around the resort along the walkways, something that should NEVER happen at a 5-star resort. Construction workers often walk through the resort in raggy attire, making you wonder about security.Many of the staff do not speak good English. Ask them something outside of the key phrases they have been trained to know and respond to, and you will often stump them.This resort could be anywhere in the world. There is nothing special about it. It is NOT A BALI experience. There is no culture here. If you want to go swimming in a big pool, eat in expensive but not so good restaurants, and stay in a decent room, then I guess the Ritz is for you. You could do that other places at a fraction of the price with better service and better ocean views/access.If you want to see the real Bali and have an experience you'll positively remember, then save your money and don't stay here.The Ritz Carlton Bali is one of the most over rated resorts in the world.

<Author>L0vesBali
<Content>What an amazing place - Magic! We have just arrived back from 5 stunning days at the Ritz Carlton in Bali. We had initially booked an ocean view suite, however when we arrived were told taht they had over booked these particular rooms so they had to upgrade us to a cliff top villa! We checked in reasonably quickly and were then escorted by hotel buggy to the villa.We entered through beautiful balinese doors to the sound of water trickling down the water feature, placed strategically near the entrance. The air temp inside the villa was very refreshing considering the sweltering heat we had experienced outside. Immediatley our eyes were drawn to the private plunge pool directly outside of the double glass doors, off the lounge area. There was also a balinese style cabana and sun lounges for you to enjoy the view. Our view was not of the ocean, however the garden sourrounding the pool area was very nice. Off the lounge area was the bedroom which had a huge king size bed, and a large plasma screen (not that there was any watching tv). From the bed, you could see outside onto the patio area and pool. It was a nice spot to lie when it got too hot outside.The most impressive part of the villa was the gigantic bathroom. It had double vanities, a changing area, a huge shower and toilet area and then the pinicle of the whole room was the huge spa bath sitting in a bay window so that you had full view of the pool while taking a bath. The bath was filled with cool water and had floating frangipani's and rose petals for beautiful presentation.My gorgeous boyfriend would pour a cool bath and a galss of wine for me each night before we went out to relax me so that I could enjoy sunset from the comfort of the bathroom!! It was heaven!The grounds of the Ritz Carton are breath-taking! It is set high on a cliff with green, soft grass areas and crystal cleaqr pools spread all over. The most impressive pool was the one which was set in the cliff side, with views spanning out over the indian ocean. From the pool you could look down to the private beach or out for miles into the ocean. It was a magical place to sit and have a cocktail by the pool in the late afternoon.We ate at the Italian restaurant on the first night we were there. The food was reasonable and the menu was quite extensive. I wouldn't rave about the food and the restaurant was quite empty, without much atmosphere so it wasn't the best night, however it was great that we could just walk from our villa to the restaurant in 5 minutes flat and not have to worry about leaving the grounds. There were some local guys serenading the few guests that were dining with U2 and Elvis Prestly. It was very sweet!My only suggestion, given that I spoke with other guests at the resort, would be to stay in a villa if at all possible. I don't think the experience would have been quite the same if we were staying in a standard room. I heard that some of the rooms are quite out dated and old and not that exciting to spend much time in.The only other problem was the fact that the hotel was quite removed from all of the action at Seminyak. It takes between 30-60 mins to travel to seminyak from the hotel, depending on the traffic. This can get quite frustrating when you are stuck in traffic which happened to us one day.My suggestion for the area of Jimbaran would be to have dinner on the beach where all the local seafood is served. You choose what you want from large water tanks and they cook it fresh on the spot. You sit directly on the sand, surrounded by many many candlelit tables. Its a very romantic and serene expereince.The other must haves in terms of dining for Seminyak would be The Living Room, Ku de ta and a cocktail at The Legian Hotel. All in all, I would say that our experience was extremely pleasant. I would go back there tomorrow given a chance. Bali is an amazing holiday destination with all the luxuries you could desire. We found that the Ritz Carlton provided everything that we had hoped for and then some. Must do it!!  
<Date>Dec 19, 2007

<Author>Vmalli
<Content>The awesome Ritz!!! There are very few resorts in the world that give the feeling that it鈥檚 worth visiting the destination just to stay in that resort. And Ritz Carlton Bali is one of them. Make no mistake; Bali in itself is a great destination -- Wonderful people, great culture, amazing architecture and fantastic restaurants. Ritz Carlton is located on a cliff overlooking the Jimbaran bay. The resort's design is impressive, Balinese-inspired -- carved stone fountains, lily ponds and low, open-air public buildings. The resort is spread over 192 acres, employees 900 people, has an awarding winning spa, 3 swimming pools, 12 restaurants and lounges, 368 rooms and 38 villas. The swimming pools are awesome especially the stunning ocean pool. The Spa is really huge and well spread out with a unique hydro therapy pool.Although the standard rooms and suites are luxuriously outfitted with marble floors and Balinese-style furnishings and fabrics, they're fairly generic -- you could be in any Ritz-Carlton in the world. Upgrades get you an ocean view, which alone make them worth springing for. The new private villas, however, with their modern and theatrical take on Balinese design -- minimalist black and beige bedroom with an enormous platform bed surrounded by flowing white curtains -- are far more dramatic. Besides their own VIP lobby and concierge area, they also boast an enormous bathroom with rain shower and sunken marble tub and a private garden with plunge pool.The service is fantastic. The staff go out of it鈥檚 way to make you feel comfortable. Location of the resort is amazing as it is located on a secluded part of Jimbaran bay on top of a cliff with views to die for. However, it鈥檚 'away' from all the action and restaurants. It鈥檚 very simple to get to Kuta and to Seminiyak from here as they are half an hour taxi ride away and by a metered taxi it will cost you just $4 - $5. The bell boys at the resort are more than happy to call for a metered taxi and that鈥檚 the cheapest and the best way to go and catch some action. The only few real drawbacks of this resort are--1. The restaurants within the resort are extremely expensive. The best thing to do to is to take a taxi ride to nearby restaurants or some of the restaurants provide free pick up and drop.2. The resort is very hilly and has lots of up's and downs - - lots steps all over the place. So if your old and your legs are weak this may not be the best option.To put it in a nutshell, I will definitely go back and recommend this incredible resort to anyone looking for a great holiday.  
<Date>Dec 4, 2007

<Author>ianwr
<Content>Simply Amazing Resort We stayed at the Ritz Carlton this September for 2 weeks which included getting married in the grounds half way through the holiday. I vowed i'd write one of these reviews when i got back so i'll try to incorporate as many of the things that i wanted to know before going and how we found it.To start off, Bali itself on initially entering the country was a little bot of a let down, when you get there make sure that you have enough hard cash to pay the visa requirement. We didn't and the cash machine rather than logically placing near where you pay for your visa is through passport control so you have to hand it in and have an armed guard escort you to the ATM and then back. Neadless to say the airport was chaos to get in and it took literally 1.5 hours to get through passport control.We got picked up by the tour company and headed off for our first drop at another hotel, even though it was a 5 star hotel its right next to pretty much shanty towns and tin huts in fact some of the back streets to get to these big hotels can look pretty mean at night. On arriving at this 1st hotel 2 machine gus where trained on us and a bomb checking guy went around the car and in the boot. I guess they are still nervous about the bombs a few years ago and it shows.To get to the ritz carlton you literally how to drive through a couple of miles of what can only describe as wasteland, including a quarry and various rubbish dumps which made us think intially what have we done and where have we gone to get married !!Security is tight on the gates of the Ritz Carlton with the same checks again but then entering past the gates is like entering a slice of paradise. It's about a further mile from the front gate to the hotel reception which is all landscaped and fragrent.That was one thing that will stick in my mind just how poor the people are outside the resort where they literally are 50 yds from the main gate in tin shacks and rubbish strewn all around to how opulant it is inside the resort.Needless to say, walking from the resort to anywhere else is pretty much out of the question and you'll need to have some transport. Taxi's are cheap though and depending on what your doing, it may well be better getting a driver for the day. We hired one through the hotel in a private air-con car for about $100 and went out for about 10 hours.We stayed in a deluxe ocean view room which was really good and had most of the things you'd expect from a 5 star hotel, there were one or two small niggles that you don't usually expect from a hotel of this calibure. Sounds strange but there was no full length mirror for my wife to get ready with, the only mirror was in the bathroom and there were no plug sockets in there to plug her straightners in s getting ready for dinner could be a struggle.Service in the hotel was second to none and the hotel staff were very friendly at all times and everything was pristine and spotless.Weather in september was the same every day, temp about 30 degress C and was usually cloudy until about lunchtime where it then cleared and you had sun until about 6pm then with sunset around 6:30pm.Prices in the hotel are reasonable but not cheap as many people make out about bali but then it is a five star hotel so you have to eexpect this especially as you are a captive audience and can't just nip out of the resort into any local shops.Water is free all day and the prices for various items are approx as follows. breakfast about 拢7.5 per person, lunchtime snack approx 拢10, dinner could range from about 拢30 per couple to upt 拢120 depending on where you ate etc. Drinks were about 拢1.50 for the local beer upto mega money for champagne. We would class ourselves as pretty average eaters and over a 2 weeks period we spent about 拢2,000 (pounds) at the resort and i would say about 拢1500 of that was on food and drink without going overboard either.There are about 5 different restaurants all exceptional in quality and we couldn't fault one thing with the food, it was exceptional every day. Othe facilities are excellent like the spa, pools, internet, gym etc. We spent 2 weeks there pretty much just in the hotel, we did venture out for the odd day or two sight seeing etc but you can easily spend this long in the hotel and not get bored if your a couple and enjoy a bit of sunbathing.I would say this isn't a hotel for a group of single sex holiday makers looking for a wild night out. The city is about 45 mins away in a taxi and there are no clubs on site just restaurants and one bar which was usually pretty much empty. It is totally geared for couples especially ones getting married. there are kids facilities on site but these are limited and to be honest i didn't see many kids at all while there.On our wedding day we got given one of the best villas for the night and the villas are totally out of this world, just fantastic. Saying that they were about $300 more per night than our existing room but if you can afford it then definately go for one. Saying that i think we got more out of the resort by staying in the main block as you are forced to visit the restaurants for dinner where in the villas you can order room service to your door and not even go out.As for weddngs, we originally were told by the estate agent that they hardly have any here and its all very special. Although it was special and they do everything they can for you its certainly not just you getting married. On our day there were two other couples getting married, we didn't see them as there are about 4 wedding venues but photo's became a problem after the ceremony at times as they don't want the brides to see each other to organise it via radio to move to certain locations when one has gone. All very funny but it limits the time you have to get your wedding shots before it goes dark.All in all i would give the resort a 5 star rating, we loved it they make everything seem special and the wedding co-ordinators are brilliant. Definately come here to get married or on honeymoon as its very quiet, very relaxing and very intimate.Don't come here if you want wild parties, nightclubs or partying until 5am each morning.Hope this review helped and if you want any other advise then just contact me.

<Author>mpolatin
<Content>Amazing Place - Great Service The photos of this place on the Ritz Website does not do it justice! This is the first time I've been to a hotel where the property was actually much better than the online photos -- just amazing pools and grounds. Probably some of the best in the world. The service was also great, but not in your face...The one downside is the beaches are not great -- you have to climb about 400 stairs down a cliff, though it is a beautiful walk and they give you cold towels and water...Also, the property is quite affordable - we paid around $200 a night (US) and were then given an opportunity to upgrade to a private condo with a plunge pool for $350 more a night. We did, and for $550 the place is unbelievable with your own private pool and waterfall -- and it is like having your own house because the place is so huge. I would warn you to make sure you get one of the good villas. Some are looking over native land where farmers and cows mingle, hurting the privacy - which is the best part of the villa. Also, the farmers sometime set fires to burn brush and this can be very annoying. The staff accommodated our request to switch villas, but we had to ask and be persistent....LAST BUT NOT LEAST, you must take at least 1 day trip around Bali and DONT go through the Ritz. Going with one of their drivers costs a fortune. WE reccomend getting a private driver that truly knows the lay of the land and the locals. We hired a driver named Dewa and he was incredible!!! GET DEWA! He was very flexible, intelligent, spoke great English, fun to hang out with and drove us around for 10 hours -- which only cost around $50 (US) for the netire day. Dewa also knows all the best spots to see monkeys, ride elephants, shop for bargains, hike etc...Dewa's website: [--]...Bali is an amazing place!

<Author>TravellerExotica
<Content>The Jewel of Jimbaran Ritz Bali is unique as it offers two drastic holiday opinions sorted out by most holiday makers all within the resort estate. It offers the commercially accessible that works well for families and the young couples. Yet within the same estate a more upscale and executive opinions are available for those that graviate towards high-end and tranquil settings. Either opinions does comes with a price tag. Our recent experience took advantage of and able to explore the different settings in a series of room/suite/villas buffets over a 9 days period. Here is our adventure.Ritz Bali EstateIts huge. The only way to bring two very different concepts within the resort is to have land. Ritz Bali had plenty of. Because its situated in Jimbaran, the resort took advantage of the coast line and incorporate this into it resort concept both in the high-end Villas and many of their restaurants. Entering the resort is telling of the size of the estate. It took a close 5 minutes car ride from the resort gates to the main reception area. There are multiple reception areas within this resort. Depending on what room you are staying in. The main reception is one that saw heavy human traffic. One you find in any commercial hotels. While the settings is very baliness with stone cravings decorated pillars, high ceilings and a small infinity pool to try welcome the more likely tired guest. The amount of guests checking in and out of the resort brings a very stressful environment. Much like what you find in a busy international airport especially during the day. In comparison the Villas reception marks a stark different to the main reception. Its set on a artifical pond with waterfall on one side, 3 piece balinese band dishing out traditional music on the other. There is often no crowd (and for the price many guests). The third reception is on an executive floor of the resort club room. While it is small its focus is executiveness. You need a keycard to access to this floor.The roomsWe are fortunate to try the three types of rooms offered; standard superior, clubroom and cliff villas. All great! The rooms are what you would find in good class business hotels with ample space, separate standing shower and a bathtub. The rooms also have a small balcony with deck chairs if you need some fresh air. Clubrooms have added compliments of fresh flowers, fruits and all the amenities you find in a deluxe room. The biggest draw of clubrooms is the club lounge access. With five food presentation throughout the day and free flow of drinks (yes wine and liquor included) it will compensate the price of the food and drinks in the resort. The service in the club lounge is great and live up to the executivity it market to be. The servers will make an effort to remember your name and your favorite drink! The food while sniplets is very nicely done. It live up to the standards of a deluxe hotel. We found clubrooms are the most value for money! So what about the villas? Having stayed in a standard room and moved to a cliff villas is like transcending from the have-not to the class of it own. First off the villas is huge with a garden and a plunge pool. It even afford personal pavillon! The villas had 3 separate space; living, bed and bathroom each of equal size! Everything is decorated with stone cravings and wood trimmings that reflects luxury. Each space had a center piece; the living room - the lounge chair; the bedroom - the 4 posterbed, the bathroom - a bathtub strategically peach with view surrounded by 3 full height window. I have not mentioned each villas comes with a 24 hour bulter service. Each double as cabby to take you anywhere within the resort compound. Because the villas are seclusively located and away from the main facilities (and crowd), you will need very much need this.The FacilitiesAs we were pampered either in the self contained villas or the club lounge, we spent little time on the compound facilities. There were a number of facilities that will awe many first timers to Bali resorts including a pool that peach next to an artifical waterfall, infinity pools, pool bars, library with internet facilities that is complimentary to villas guests, a small beach if you willing to climb the steps and of course a great frontage of the India Ocean. These however while great nice-to-have will likely not impress many seasoned resort goers especially if you been to Bali a number of times. Many of these facilities are situated at or near the hotel wing so do expect to share the treasured finds with lots of crowd. There is a well established spa within the resort compound (as in most good Bali resorts). The pride of the spa is the Rock which had a spa pavillon on a rock island. This too has a price tag that will likely set you way back. What's commentable are the complimentary facilities within the spa compound like saunas and the jacuzzi pool that set within a cavelike enclosure. These are open to resort guests.The BreakfastI would usually not single this as a segment in my feedback on a resort I visit. For Ritz Bali I would need to first for the resort to improve on and potential guests to know there are smarter options. All standard room guests will be directed during check-in to Padi (The Thai Restaurant) for breakfast. You know you are the standard room guests if your room is on the left of main entrance of the two wing hotel. If you are here is the hint. Padi offers buffet-style breakfast with a good spread. The restaurant however can not take the close to two hundred rooms house guests at one time. Be there very early and prepare for a queue. Like guests before us that left comments there are usual rush for food and occasions the kitchen cannot cope. We did explore after our first day and realize the Italian restaurant do offer seat-down breakfast. Of course you have less variety but it keep your blood pressure within safety limits. Now for club level and villas guests you will not have this problem. Club guest get to dine in the lounge which first off is more quiet and orderly. The breakfast choices are the same as those in Padi. Villas guest get to dine in Davo. The Fusion restaurant. Its a seat-down breakfast but you can order whatever on the menu as long as your stomach have the room for. Davo is an award winning restaurant so expect a great breakfast. I truly can't help after our first mad rush breakfast experience and moved to better grade rooms/villas to feel sorry for the rest of guest in the standard rooms. Readers do be warned. This is one situation where a choice of rooms do help.Dinning ConceptsLike any good resorts that wanted more of inhouse guest dollars, Ritz Bali had come up with a number of creative dinning concepts to entice its guests. To take a step further it has a restaurant deskfront within the reception to help guests select the best dinning concepts. As Ritz Bali is a popular wedding and honeymoon spot, the concepts are both interesting and refreshing. First off there are six restaurants to spoil the choice of inhouse guests. It ranges from Thai, Italian, Japanese, Fusion and Seafood. Many are award winning restaurants. Each will dish out very respectable fine dinning experience. The price is also set at that range too. You need to be mentally prepared your dinning experience as one you likely would have and paid for in a high-end restaurant back home. The service is up to that mark too. Several prior commentary were made with comparsion to local Bali experience which is a faction of those in Kuta or Legian. Ritz commands this because it fully optimize nature backdrop as part of the dinning experience. Take Pesta Lobster Dinning. Its set on a jetty with only one table for two, with full attendance of a dedicated bulter and a three piece band that dish out traditional balinese muisc throughout your dinning. You get to view the famous Jimbaran sunset all by yourself. For such experience prepare to cough out slightly more then five hundred USD (inclusive 21% tax) for the three hour without wine. A word of caution to fully understand what each dinning concept entails as some may sound interesting initially but may not turn out what you would envisioned. We did try three of their four speciality concepts and not really liking every one. Of course we paid plenty to try in the first place. Another area that guests need to be aware is prices of wine is higher then what you can get and what I as a wine lover is somewhat disappointed is the selections are limited and not the range that would you would expect for the price, whichever part of the world you come from. We had foresight to get two bottles of exquisite wine on our way to Bali. Corkage is affordable and would be a better option if you, like me crave to compliment your food with good wine.Overall Ritz Bali has the glamour and resort charm. Our trip is most pleasant and very much enjoyable. Of course we need to get back to reality and starting patching the hole in our pocket!

<Content>Loved it - Wonderful Honeymoon! Our recent honeymoon at the Ritz Carlton in Bali was beyond amazing. The service was impeccable and the food was delicious. Of course the food and drinks are much more expensive at the resort than outside in the local towns, but it was worth it to enjoy the excellent service and convenience of staying at the resort. We stayed our first 7 nights in a Deluxe Ocean View Suite - the room was beautiful and we had turndown service every night (in addition to regular room cleanings). There are not too many TV channels there, but who needs TV when you're in such a beautiful location? Our last 4 nights were spent in a Private Villa - total luxury. The private beach at the Ritz was definitely a hike, but well worth it once you arrived down there (recommend that you bring some snacks with you). We did not book where the morning breakfast was included (which made it pricey for us - about $30-$35 pp!) so we would recommend booking where your breakfast is included (a majority of guests seemed to have this option). Sunset cocktails in front the pool were superb, you can't beat the views. Sami-Sami had wonderful Italian food, we ate there a couple of times. Zen had some of the most amazing sushi we've ever had, we ate there a couple times as well and highly recommend it. We enjoyed it all, it was a truly amazing honeymoon and we can't wait to go back.

<Author>Miciogatto
<Content>Loved the Ritz Carlton Bali I have recently spend 4 nights at the Ritz Carlton in Bali. I'd like to give a few advice:1. book a Club room if you do not have children under 12: the rooms are new with nice furniture, great view, big plasma TV, large bathroom with separate shower and little balcony. If you stay at the Club you have separate check-in and out (important in this very crowded hotel!!!), five food presentations every day (you could really eat only at the Club lounge, where you have breakfast, midday snack, afternoon tea, aperitifs and after dinner spirits and chocolates), newspapers.2. do not miss the two beaches of the hotel: one is right below the main pool, after a few stairs, with nice restaurant and bar, infinity pool with seawater and nice day-beds. The other one is in another bay, you have to go 185 steps down (I think they are even more...) but once you are there it is like paradise. Only a small menu with lots of drinks or if you want picnic baskets prepared and delivered to you on the beach in an hour. The staff is really nice and helpful. They call you by name (not easy in hotels so big and crowded)3. do not miss the experience of the hydrotherapy at the main pool of the Spa. Even if they charge you $40 it's a unforgettable experience especially at sunset. A real magic place.4. Try the Japanese restaurant (fully renovated) which offer a sushi bar, a Teppaniaki and a Korean barbecue: expensive but excellent quality5. try the new restaurant Dava, at the Villa area, after an aperitif at the Martini Bar: both these places are new, with excellent staff, nice view and good food. Expensive, yes, but really romantic.6. do not go at this Ritz Carlton if you look for a hotel with international guests. It seems there are only Japanese and Korean: they said 70% of the guests, I'd say 95%. The other 5% European (German, Spanish, Italian).

<Author>Tracie58712
<Content>What a Place!!! If you're are anything like me, you visit TripAdvisor almost every day before you leave to see if there were any new reviews on the hotel you chose to stay in in Bali. Because of that, I'll try to comment on everything about this amazing resort.Prior to our departure, we confirmed airport pickup though the hotel's online request service. Imagine our surprise when we exited the doors of the airport and saw dozens of people holding papers with names on them, but none of them ours. Yeah, it was a bit interesting/stressful, to say the least. Thankfully we found a phone and called the resort, who said that the shuttle would be there in 5 minutes. This was interesting, too, since our flight actually was a bit delayed. No sooner after we hung up the phone, a guy with a sign Ritz-Carlton found us and ushered us into the van. Fortunately, this airport snafu wasn't indicative of the hotel and our stay.There was a bottle of champagne for us as we made our way to the resort. It was part of our package and a really cool touch. When we pulled up to the hotel, security checked all around the vehicle, and then lifted the gate for us to drive the 1KM to the front of the resort. Upon arrival, we were greeted with a fragrant lei, some wonderful juice (pineapple guava? we never figured out what it was exactly), and a cold towel that had been soaked in frangipani. Check-in was seamless, and we were taken to our room (1326) right away. The room was amazing. We had an ocean view deluxe room, and contemplated upgrading to a villa, but ultimately decided that the room we were given was nice enough (plus, we didn't want to spend $300 more/night!!!). Their was a canopy bed with crisp white linens, a flat screen TV, yummy bedside snacks, a Bose speaker system with iPod capabilities, a nice tub with floating flowers, and robes waiting for us. The only thing I could possibly fault about the room was the lack of an alarm clock, or even a clock for that matter. It got to be annoying having to keep asking my husband what time it was (I'm sure for him, too!). As others have mentioned, the walls were kinda thin, but this didn't seem to be a problem for us, as we were awake and asleep at the same times as the people around us. I can see how this might be a problem for some though.The hotel grounds are simply amazing. The landscaping, flowers, carvings, etc. are all so beautiful. The attention to detail is unparalleled. They have thought of everything and execute it all wonderfully. Every single staff member, from reception to the grounds crew, has a smile on his/her face, and is eager to greet you with a good morning/afternoon/evening. The grounds are pretty vast... I think 80hectacres, but we didn't find anything to be too far to walk. There is a complimentary shuttle at the front for those who don't want to walk, though.We had breakfast every morning at Padi. The spread was great and there was something for everyone. Have the hazelnut brioche... you won't be disappointed!! We had dinner one night at Padi, also, and were highly impressed with the Thai cuisine. Don't miss out on the banana crisps for dessert. They are SO worth it!! Trust me. We dined one night at Sami Sami and were impressed with the Italian food. Actually, the food everywhere at the resort was amazing. I don't think you could get a bad dish. Their food and beverage operations are phenomenal. We were fortunate enough to use the spa facilities three times during our stay. The first treatment we received was a Balinese massage and was a part of our package. The treatment was nice, but neither my room nor my husbands had music, which was kinda odd. I don't know if this was a fluke or what, but the music was on during our other treatments. I had the Ritz Supermodel package, a Thermes Firming facial, and a manicure and my husband had a reflexology treatment. The spa is great. After you check-in, you are given some more of that wonderful pineapple/guava juice and then ushered into the locker room, which was equipped with everything you would need after your treatment. The spa rooms were spacious and nice. Gung-In was my therapist for two treatments and I highly recommend her. Following the treatment, you receive a Balinese cake and either water or lime juice, depending on the time of the day. The hotel offers many activities that you might want to take advantage of. We took the hotel shuttle out to Kuta one day. There are only 11 spots on the shuttle, so if you want to leave at a certain time, make sure you request it with the concierge. We also hired a taxi that took us out to the Uluwatu temples. Be careful of the monkeys.. we saw a guy lose his glasses to them while we were there. Also, be cautious of anyone who seems official and tries to take you around the grounds on a guided tour. Chances are, they are not and will expect a tip after speeding you through the grounds. We learned this the hard way. Go around 5PM and stay for the traditional dance that starts at 6PM. The taxi has a three-hour minimum, so this is perfect. We spent most of our time at the ocean pool, which is not to be confused with the Kubu private beach, although we did spend one day there, as well. The ocean pool is located down a bunch of steps (141 if I recall correctly) and is an infinity pool. There aren't many spots for people to lay out by the pool, so it's quieter than other spots around the resort. Don't worry about bringing a towel to the pool; two towels are provided and a Ritz staff member will unroll it and set up your chair for you once you get there. As soon as someone leaves, they replace the towels. We booked a picnic lunch down at Kubu beach one day. It's quite a workout getting down to the beach. Something like 191 steep steps. The ocean is nice, but too strong to swim in, so it's more just for relaxing. Take the hotel shuttle to the entrance... it's quite a walk if you don't. Walking back up the steps is where the challenge comes in! This resort was amazing and we are so lucky that we were afforded the opportunity to stay here. I will admit that I was a bit nervous and anxious about traveling to Bali, but after staying here and getting to know some of the local people, I didn't want to leave! Have a great time!!

<Author>bbbs
<Content>Beautiful Grounds Possibly one of the best hotels in terms of landscaping that we鈥檝e ever visited. The grounds are extremely beautiful, with eye pleasing architecture infused with simple Balinese accents. The staff is extremely gracious and speaks extremely good English, they never hesitate to greet you when they pass by. Our room was not ready when we arrived because the entire hotel seemed to be almost fully booked, but we just spent the time exploring the grounds. Initially we were given a room on the first floor, however, it was completely adjacent to the mini golf course and the area for garbage disposal (?! Why they even have a room near there is beyond me) so we called and were able to change rooms swiftly and without any problems (once again the staff were very helpful). The room itself is not spectacular, however the floor is marble and the TV is a huge flat screen. Bathroom came with a tub and separate walk in shower and toilet, everything was extremely clean and the hairdryer is probably one of the most efficient I鈥檝e ever used. The Ritz has 4 pools: 3 of them on the main hotel area, and the last, a hike down to near the beach. The main pool is an infinity pool: long and rectangular, good for swimming laps and taking pictures out towards the sea. This infinity pool falls over into another pool below it which is more for paddling around in. The children鈥檚 pool off to the side is complete with small water slides. The last pool was our favorite, the hike was not very taxing at all (though it does involve a large number of stairs so those with difficulty climbing stairs should beware), but the beauty and serenity of the pool completely makes up for it. There are even small, covered cabanas staggered on levels leading to the pool if you just want to lie in the sun or watch the ocean if all the lounge chairs on the pool deck are full. The staff even came around with skewers of cold fruit and squirt bottles filled with cold water to keep us cool. The breakfast buffet was decent, with choices sure to satisfy all tastes, from asian to western, but if your room does not come with free breakfast it may not be worth it. The spa and fitness center was well equipped and had very pleasant and accommodating staff. The only downside to this hotel perhaps, is its isolation from鈥?well, frankly, everything. Though there is a stretch of beachside restaurants nearby, it is more than a 2 km walk. And the town of Kuta is more than a 15 minute car ride. The hotel does provide a shuttle but only 4 times a day with only 1 trip per time, each trip being able to hold only 10 people, so you must book in advance. But for those who came to Bali to sunbathe and relax, the Ritz is an amazing place for it.

<Author>luxury-lizard
<Content>Ritz - some good and some not so good stuff My husband and I just returned from Bali where we spent 6 nights at the RC at Jimbaran and then 6 nights at The Viceroy in Ubud (see separate review). The RC is quite nice - it has spectacular gounds and very nice pool areas (as per other reivews) as well as a private beach which is wonderful albiet down 184 steep stairs.The RC is however quite far from other hotels / towns - at least 20 minutes by taxi (taxis are cheap and plentiful but it can be a bit of a drag not to be able to walk anywhere). The restaurants are good (not great) and charge 5* prices (as do all other 5* hotels in Bali).After the first night in a standard room (which had partial ocean views and had been redecorated) we opted for a Club Room at $170 extra pn - it was an identical room with full ocean views but the Club extras simply were not worth the additional money.I had 3 spa treatments and they were top notch - again US$$ prices. My one gripe is that the famous hydroponic pools at the sps cost an additional $40 per person per 2 hour visit - quite OTT.The RC's top restaurant is Dava - located in the villa area - it has a spectacular setting and excellent (eclectic) food. As an aside we went to Ku De Ta one evening for dinner (in Seminyak) - and it's a great overall experience - try it !!

<Author>TokyoSurferboy
<Content>Good but not great Stayed at the Ritz for 4 days in April but were not too excited about it. Weather was bad - thunderstorms and constant raining (of course not the Ritz' fault). We have been to Bali many a times (4 Seasons, Melia, Sofitel, Oberoi, Club at Legian, etc) but were a little bit disappointed about the Ritz and its location.Plus: Overall architecture is very nice; main pool area beautiful and fun to hang around; drinks/food service good and staff are attentive. Accomodation - room was OK but nothing to be excited about. Probably wouldn't stay at the Ritz again due to prices and limited location.
