<Author>zermatt2002
<Content>A big bang for less than USD200/night! We stayed at a resort view room for four nights in May 2007. It was such a fantastic experience that we felt sad leaving the hotel. We were very disappointed with Bali in general and the Kuta beach in particular, but the Ritz-Carlton Bali was definitely the highlight of our trip. We ended up staying inside the hotel properties most of our time in Bali. We traveled extensively around the world, but the Ritz-Ccarlton Bali still amazes us. Considering that we paid only about USD 187/night, I doubt that one could find a better deal elsewhere in the world. If you have a deep pocket, go for a cliff villa. Otherwise, stay in a resort view room and you get to use the magnificiant pools and wander around the tastefully designed tropical gardens. You get the picture. Ritz Bali is a perfect place for total relaxation. Classy, secluded and most importantly, affordable. 1) Room: Since we booked the cheapest room type, we didn't expect too much. The room is not that new by Asian standards, but it's spacious, the amenities are good and there are housekeeping twice a day. We were lucky to get a room right by the golf course. What a view!2) Facilities: There're two major pools. One is an infinity pool at the heart of the hotel ground, and the other is a river pool. Most people gether around the ifinity pool to see the ocean view. I like the river pool better. Very few people actually went that far to the river pool. I was the only person swimming. I felt like swimming in my own private pool! The river pool was sooooo stunning that we spent half of the day there and went back twice. 3) Services: Services are impeccable! Staff always greet you with a smile and are willing to go out their way to help you. If you have time, don't forget to take the free shuttle to the Kubu private beach. 4) Restaurants: We only went to Padi, where breakfast was served by the beautiful lily pond. Padi was rated as the best restaurant in Indonesia. I'm not surprised. The Japanese and Indonesian breakfast were artfully cooked! If possible, try to have your breakfast included in your hotel package. (It's about USD 30/person if it's not included in the package.) Restaurants inside the hotel are expensive even by New York standards. The only exception is the buffet dinner (USD 55 +21% tax) ) that is offered outdoors once a week. It sounds expensive, but it's a bargain. You see the Balinese dance show. For our lunch, we took the 11:30 AM free shuttle to Kuta to sample a wide array of Indonesian food at much lower prices. We took the 3:45 PM shuttle back to the hotel. I gave Ritz Bali a 95 on a scale of 100. (The minus 5 goes to the inhibitive food prices.)

<Author>chinagirl
<Content>Spectacular We stayed here for six days in February and had a fantastic time. We had an ocean view room with a very large bathrooom and a deck overlooking the ocean. The hotel is simply gorgeous. We particularly liked spending time at the beach (2km away and down 180 steps so very uncrowded) and the ocean pool, which is set on a cliff overlooking the Indian Ocean and is stunning. However it was really the service which made our stay so enjoyable. The staff constantly seemed so happy to see us and genuinely welcoming such that their cheerful moods were contagious. Although the hotel was full for Chinese New Year, the grounds are so vast that it was able to accomodate all of the guests without feeling crowded. The food was delicious, both at breakfast and other meals, especially in the Thai restaurant. We used the gym quite a bit, and took advantage of the daily yoga classes, but never made it to the spa, which we plan to do on our next visit. The location and vastness of the resort makes it hard to leave the grounds easily, but this remoteness also feels very relaxing. It is close to the fish barbeques on Jimabarn beach which we went to one night and really enjoyed.

<Author>Musken
<Content>Great resorts Had a wonderful stay at the Ritz Carlton, Bali i february 2006. 12 nights. ROOMSWe were lucky to get an upgrade to one of the Cliff Villas which were absolutely wonderful. Beautiful living room and bedroom, though could have wished for more light in the living room as it was pretty dark at night. Quiet and effective aircondition. Very comfortable bed. Fantastic and huge bathroom, really the best I have ever seen, (and I am a bathroom freak and have stayed in several Aman resorts) including big walk in wardrobe, and amazing bathtub. Lots of storage space. Fantastic outside area with bale, private pool, and huge garden with loads of beautiful flowers. SERVICEMainly very good, though could have been absolutely excellent with small improvements. RESTAURANTSSpecial breakfast restaurants for villas closed during our stay so we had to eat at the main restaurant. No problem, though. Very good selection during breakfast, though sometimes waiting time before we could get seated. Normally we did not have lunch since breakfast was huge. Dinner options very good: Absolutely great thai restaurant, fantastic fusion restaurant, good fish restaurant, italian restaurant with very good pizzas and OK pasta. We had all dinners in the hotel and never felt that this was boring. Indonesian buffet restaurant outside where shows etc. was going to take place was closed, which was a bit of a disappointment. Room service very good, though a bit limited choice. POOLSVery good. Choice between main pool and other pool for villa guests only, latter being very quiet. Very good and attentive service at pool areas. CHILDREN ACTIVITIESNot a lot of kids there. Our son (2,5 years back then) was too young to join the kids club, but was more than welcome to play there with us when he wanted. Good kids menu in all restaurants, also providing healthy options, not just junk food. BEACHNot quite the same style as the rest of the hotels (plastic beds) but excellent service. We had a pre ordered lunch basket at the beach which was excellent. Loads of food and very tasty. OTHERSSome waiting time for the little cars to take us from villa to rest of hotel area. Some of the butlers really good, others only OK. No insects. They were spraying almost every 2nd day over the whole area.

<Author>Ellen43
<Content>Fabulous Villas We stayed in the main hotel for two nights and then moved to the villas for two more. The hotel is nice but the rooms are nothing to write home about, and from some vantage points you really can't see much of the ocean (our first ocean view room afforded about a thumbnail of Indian Ocean--if that). However, the villa was wonderful. It is difficult to describe how nice without actually seeing it--gorgeous, extremely comfortable, with a very serene pool and patio. The grounds throughout the resort were lovely. But perhaps the best thing is the new cliff-side sea water swimming pool which has an infinity edge that overlooks the ocean and was, quite simply, amazing. The staff were all extremely nice. The downside of the whole south Bali resort area is that it feels rather disconnected and you don't get to see a whole lot of the rest of Bali without some effort. It is so westernized, I kept thinking that I may as well have been in Hawaii.

<Author>EalingMember
<Content>Excellent Hotel  Having booked the Ritz Carlton Bali based on reviews on this site, we departed the UK with an air of concern at the some of the recent negative comments about the hotel. However, we can honestly say that for our entire stay (10 days) the staff, service and facilities were superb.We chose to stay in one of the Club Level Rooms and made good use of the Club Lounge and the services of the welcoming and attentive staff. The entire team went out of their way to remember your name and preferences. The food and beverages served in the lounge were excellent and the small library of books available was a useful addition.Restaurants: Very good mix of restaurants offering a broad selection of food. Kisik was a particular favourite offering fresh seafood and an excellent setting. Prices in the restaurants are comparable to other 5 star hotels.Swimming Pool: The hotel has a myriad of pools to service all tastes. If you want peace a quiet then head for the villa pool or the newly opened ocean pool. During the day staff bring you cold towels, fruit and a small smoothy!Gym: The gym has a good mix of machines and free weights and doesn't get overcrowded. The staff will also give you a good stretch is you ask. Aerobic and yoga classes are also available. Golf: The mini- 18 hole golf course is excellent and well worth a round or two.Spa: Apparently the biggest in Asia, the Spa is fantastic and offers an impressive list of treatments. The bali massage and facials were both very good. However the aquatonic pool is a must. TIP: Go to the aquatonic pool around 4:30pm so you can catch the sunset whilst going round the different elements. Beach: Kuba Beach is very nice though we would recommend you take a shuttle car to get there unless you want a long walk. Also there is no lift to the beach, so you will need to be fit to climb the 180 steps. Grounds: Set in 70+ hectacres the resort is massive. Therefore despite the hotel being 90% full the resort did not feel overcrowded.Tours: Whilst external taxi's are available at the hotel, we chose to use the hotel cars and driver for our excursions round the island. The price is a lot higher but you get a betterquality car, the driver speaks good english and knows some good places to visit, and the hotel provide you with a basket of cold drinks and towels. Places to Visit: See the sunset at the Uluwatu Temple and then head over to Nusa Dua for a meal at Bumbu Bali. We highly recommend this hotel. Don't be put off by the location -taxi's are very cheap and feely available if you want to spend some time away from the resort.

<Author>Aqa
<Content>the basics needed improvement.... I have just returned from a stay at the Ritz Carlton in Bali, not in a villa, but in a deluxe ocean view room.I share the comments made by previous trip advisor members, the sound-proofing of the hotel can definitely be improved. From our first room, we could hear footsteps outside, conversations, and at 6am in the morning, footsteps from the floor above. Our second room was at the end of one of the wings, and hence was a lot quieter.I found the staff very willing to help, courteous, and always all smiles. However, I think the basics of the hotel requires improvement. I.e. I used the reqest a service function on the website to ask about transportation from the airport, and I received no reply for 3 days, despite the 24hrs turnaround time promised. We switched rooms whilst we were there, and the amenities provided seems to vary with each room, one provides a 'do not disturb' sign, whilst another does not. One has a bedside clock, whilst another doesn't. Housekeeping is also a bit careless, i.e. they forgot to replace the bathtowels one night, and the other, they took away used coffee mugs without replacing them. Our request for items to be brought to the room is also not always responded to quickly.Another thing to pay attention to is the breakfast buffet. Some of the food is not covered, i.e. fruit, coldcuts, butter etc. I picked up a bit of food poisoning on the last day, and had a very miserable journey back home. The pool and the views in the hotel is fantastic. I would still recommend the hotel, but i think your experience really depends on the room you get.

<Author>chrispt
<Content>Perfect setting for wedding in Bali We got married at the Ritz Carlton on August 25th and stayed a total of 15 nights - so, we have quite a bit of feedback - all of it very complimentary, I hasten to add! From the initial queries in Feb/March time to the day we left, I have to say the hotel were superb in every aspect. From a wedding perspective, the wedding co-ordinators, Karlina and Imelda, bent over backwards to ensure everything went smoothly and that all arrangements were carried out prior to arrival. The day itself exceeded our expectations - helped by having the best sunset in the two week stay! - and the staff certainly made it a very memorable occasion. Regarding the hotel itself, it was perfect for what we wanted. Very relaxed atmosphere throughout. The staff were always happy and smiling and loved it if you could speak a bit of the language with them. We booked an Executive room and to anyone thinking about upgrading, it is definitely worthwhile. If you wanted to, you could eat all your meals in the Executive Lounge and not bother about eating out! I know this sounds lazy, but believe me, a lot of people do it (mainly the Koreans and Japanese). The food is excellent and plentiful; drinks are available all day - yes, some people were even drinking beer at breakfast time! The room was large and had a great sea view; excellent shower and hotel products. The pools are lovely - we preferred the pool by the spa villas, only because it was quieter. The spa was superb as well and the treatments reasonably priced. The bars are great for relaxing late in the evening. The Thai restaurant was very good - we didn't try out the others. We did go into Jimabaran though a few times to try one of the 150 beach-side fish restaurants, which was also good value and great entertainment - taxi only takes about 10 minutes and costs around IDR 25,000 (about 拢1.40) - well worth it! The grounds are beautifully kept and the flowers are stunning. The private beach is well worth the long climb up and down. All in all, we could not fault the hotel! For us though, it was the hotel staff who really made our stay - they were courteous, polite, charming and above all genuine. I would be happy to answer any questions about the hotel and specifically about planning a wedding at the Ritz Carlton.

<Author>therobster
<Content>Can't get the basics right My wife and I went to Bali for our honeymoon, and planned to stay at the Bali Hyatt for 5 days, then at the Ritz-Carlton for 5 days. The Hyatt impressed us with fantastic service, but we had the impression the Ritz would be even better. And at twice the price we were expecting great things. Unfortunately this wasn't the case.We had planned to stay in one of the regular rooms. When you book, you make your own decisions on what you can and what you want to spend on your holiday, right? But upon check-in at the Ritz you are made to feel that if you don't upgrade to a villa you're not really going to be having a good time. Great way to welcome someone.The room was good, nice view, good size and clean. So then we went down to the pool to grab a quick lunch and have a swim. So we both ordered a chicken burger, nothing fancy, from the surly pool boy. 30 minutes later they arrived. No kidding. I am pretty sure you could slaughter, pluck and mince (yes it was minced chicken, not a fillet) a chicken in 30 minutes. So far so not impressed.We then thought we'd have a quick go on the putting golf course. When we got to hole 6 we heard this...noise. Someone was spraying chemicals on the plants about 25m away, forming a cloud that eventually enveloped half of the resort. Seriously it looked like 'Nam out there, and smelt worse. This was 4pm on a Friday afternoon...?We went down later to eat dinner. One of the restaurants was closed for a function. They weren't interested in showing us where another restaurant was.We eventually found a place to eat which looked nice, on the lawn overlooking the sea. Upon being shown to our table we realised it was a set dinner, no a la carte. No problem - but why couldn't the maitre'd inform us before taking the trouble to sit us down? We ordered a bottle of Cabernet Sauvignon, which came, surprisingly, chilled. Hmm. When we returned to our room we found out that we had been put next to a family with 3 young kids, kicking up a racket. The management knew we were on honeymoon, so why do this?We moved rooms, and asked the bellboy if he could get us a teapot for our room while he was moving the bags. He told us to call room service. Why not offer to do it for us?In general the staff seem to be badly trained, not very proficient at English, not very friendly and not very happy to be there. The best thing the Ritz-Carlton did for us (after complaining to the manager) was arrange a car for us to go straight back to the Bali Hyatt the next day! The Ritz-Carlton tries to be all about luxury, and the setting is indeed luxurious and must have cost a fortune to build. But they've forgotten a key ingredient, which is service. They can't even get the basics right, and at this price that's a serious mistake. Avoid.  
<Date>Oct 8, 2006

<Author>Julesee
<Content>Generally nice but make sure you stay in a Villa! Generally a nice resort, but initially we were put in one of the rooms in the main building where unfortunately the sound proofing leaves a little to be desired. In the first room we were allocated we could hear the footsteps rather too loudly, while in the second we could hear the neighbours through the adjoining door. This quality of sound proofing is not what you would expect from a five star hotel - the noise sensitive should be very wary! Also, the main building was frankly not particularly beautiful. One other minor complaint was that the staff are constantly trying to get you to go to one of the hotel restaurants - when it happens once or twice a day, fine, but when it happens five or six that's a bit much.However, we were moved to a villa and that was really nice - here we found the privacy that was lacking elsewhere.The food was very good at the RC. Dava was a particularly nice gourmet restaurant, while the Thai themed one was top notch too. The buffer dinner and Balinese dance on the Wednesday was very good - and the best dance we saw while in Bali. Breakfast was pretty good, as were the poolside snacks. As for external restaurants, we enjoyed a decent Friday buffet dinner (six on the beach) at the four seasons, while La Lucciola was a good italian in Seminyak. It's also well worth going to dinner at one of the fish restaurants on the beach at Jimbaran bay.We did a lot of shopping for antiques and handicrafts. It's well worth checking some of the antique and handicraft shops in Seminyak, Kerobokan and near Jimbaran bay. Particularly worth checking out is Cempaka near the Bali Galleria near Jimbaran, plus a lot of the wholesale outlets on the same road. Cempaka is not cheap, but their mix of main comtempary crafts, furniture and ceramics were the most interesting we saw while there.

<Author>mogu
<Content>Wonderful Ritz Carlton We stayed at the Ritz for 3 nights this April.We got a sea view room which was spacious, elegant and very clean.The pools are nicely located and have a magnificent view of the ocean. The breakfasts are delicious, and we especially recommend the waffles.The shops inside the Ritz have very good taste. They have stylish bags, accessories, swimwear, and all sorts of souvenirs. Although it is pricey by Bali standards, the quality is top-notch.What was best about the Ritz were the people working there. Whenever you pass by one of the staffs, they will give you a warm smile which reassures that you are welcome at this beautiful place. If you ask for something, they will be swift and efficient, always pleased to help you.DOs and DON'Ts in Ritz and / or Jimbaran:Dos:Watch the Kecak dance at the Uluwatu Temple.You can watch the beautiful sunset while enjoying the traditional Kecak dance.Try the Spa inside the Ritz. We did the couple's package treatment named Cinta Abadi.We were shown into a beautiful and spacious Spa Room exclusively for this package.Both the treatment and atmosphere were excellent. It was heaven! DON'Ts:Do not go to, or should I say beware of rip-off seafood restaurants in Jimbaran.Jimbaran is known for their delicious seafood restaurants, but some of those restaurants include ones which are tourist trap rip-off joints.The one we went to was called Jimbaran Bay Cafe or JBC where for one lobster and some fish (which were not even so good) cost us US$130. This price is extremely overpriced for Bali standards.If you choose the right place with the adequate prices, you should have a good time.

<Author>balimontana
<Content>Best in Bali During 2003 - 2004 I had the pleasure of living in the Ritz Carlton Bali for nine months while constructing my own private villa property in Bali.Simply put, the Ritz Carlton Bali is the best hotel on the island. The villas at the Ritz Carlton are large and very well appointed. The 24 hour Butler service offered to villa guests is beyond compare. The Butlers will bend over backwards to fulfill special requests and take great pride in their job.Since I have a vacation home in Bali, I know most all of the luxury hotels on the island and know their villas. The Ritz Carlton villas are the nicest and offer the best service and best value for money in my opinion.The spa at the Ritz Carlton Bali is the best I've ever been to with the Spa at the Grand Wailea in Maui running a distant second. The Ritz Carlton Bali spa features a huge Thalassotherapy pool which after two hours leaves you more relaxed and refreshed than imaginable. The spa facility is very large and luxurious.Dining too is a delight with recently opened Aqua and Padi Thai restaurant offering world class dining within the resort facility.The resort does offer regular rooms and suites. I recommend these if you are on a budget and still want to experience the amazing facilities of the hotel. The suites in particular offer great value for money. The classic Ritz Carlton Club Lounge is on offer here and the Club Lounge in Bali compares very favorably to other Ritz Carlton Clubs with ample and delicious food and beverage presentations on offer 5 times daily. The Club Lounge and Suites offer great value for money.Highly recommended for a very memorable vacation! It was an amazing experience living in this property for nine months.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Wonderful service and beautiful gardens We just returned from the Ritz near Jimberan Bay after a very relaxing stay. The first thing that struck me on this my first trip to Bali was how amazingly friendly the people are. This goes for the hotel staff as well as others we met on the island during our stay. We were upgraded to a villa which was a very pleasant surprise. The bathrooms are fabulous and you have your own private plunge pool and bale (and a butler should you need it!). The hotel grounds are beautifully maintained and the main pool is also very pleasant with an abundance of comfy sun loungers. The hotel is set high up on a cliff top just away from Jimberan Bay and it has its own private beach, although some might not be keen on the 150 steps down to it, but it's not far and there's a botle of cool water waiting for you at the top and a buggy to take you back to your room. One of the advantages of Jimberan over Nusa Dua (where we also stayed on this trip) is that you get to see the sun set over the sea. We had an excellent meal at the Dava restaurant and a more average one at the Thai restaurant. I would recommend a mix of eating at the hotel and also getting a taxi a short ride to Jimberan and eating at one of the many excellent beachside restaurants there. The hotel was fairly empty because of the recent tragic events in the area, but we felt totally safe and were very glad that we didn't cancel our tip. The photos on the Ritz website don't do the hotel justice, it's a lovely place.

<Author>Crosby1
<Content>Kick Back and Relax Your Days Away My wife and I have just returned to Vancouver, Canada on October 1st from five days at the Ritz-Carlton, Bali; just one day after the bombs went off on the island, so our hearts go out to the Balinese and tourists alike who were killed or injured in the two, separate areas of Bali.It is hard to write about such an idyllic place when there has been recent violence but we would certainly return to support the Balinese who made our stay so wonderful and to enjoy what has to be one of the best managed five-star resort hotels in Asia-Pacific. It is important to note that the Ritz Carlton Hotel is a fully secured site. When we arrived at the hotel, guards stopped our taxi (and other cars too) at the main gate and checked the under the cars using mirrors before allowing vehicles to proceed down a very long entrance driveway to where we were greeted by the friendly and helpful staff of the hotel.I would encourage anyone staying at the Ritz-Carlton Bali to pay the extra hundred dollars a day and get a room in the Club Level. Our room looked out over the ocean (a distance away) but was spacious, immaculate and beautiful. We were escorted to our room and the bath tub was filled with fragrant flowers floating in water (the entire guest room is fully marbled to keep things crisp and cool and ensures there is no mildew from the humdity)and there were also flower petals laid out on the bed along with robes and slippers by the side of the bed. Fresh fruit was waiting along with a note from the management about how the Club Room offered tennis and the special mini-golf at no charge, along with some discounts on dry-cleaning (a must in humid Bali).The real value, though, is in the Club Lounge where each morning you are greeted by name, taken to a table in the air-conditioned Lounge and then have a choice of fruit, cereals, various breads and croissants plus your own chef preparing omlettes. If you are Asian, there is a special buffet available too. The Lounge offers snacks near Noon, Afternoon Tea (with finger sandwiches and scones plus fruit) and evening drinks and hors d'oeuvres and a late night snack too. Great if you want a cold bottle of water or juice anytime of the day given it is so hot (30+C)and humid.We had dinner at all the restaurants on-site except the Japanese spot which seemed over-priced. Dava is very modern and minimalist while Sami-Sami and Padi are outdoors, very romantic and all have wonderful food. Try the Martini Bar adjacent to Dava and watch the sun go down. Prices are good in terms of international hotels. Maybe a bit more expensive that other places in Bali but let me assure you the attention to detail is amazing and the food is truly outstanding.The pool areas (there are actually three on site) are great and the view from the main infinity pool is truly amazing. The Spa is is wonderful and how can anyone not try a real Balinese massage given by a person who grew up on Bali and who truly cares about their work. More than anything though are the service levels. Lots of staff who are eager to please and who go out of their way to make sure you are happy. Even the fellow pushing the laundry cart down the corridor says hello and asks how you are this morning/afternoon...and he is sincere. Wouldn't it be nice to have such attentive service in North America? We took a 6-hour tour using a hotel car and driver (ask for Peno, he is wonderful) and it only costs $15 per hour and it was worth every penny given the way people drive on Bali and how Peno takes you off the beaten path to the less commercial part of Bali.Finally, I realize this kind of hotel experience is not for everyone. We went after attending business meetings in Kuala Lumpur, so our desire was for five days of reading books, relaxing and not climbing into the hills of Bali. If you want night-life then this is not the place. If, however, you want a first-class hotel with all the trimmings, then this is the place to go. You will be treated right and want to return as the staff waves 'good-bye' to you as you head back to the airport.

<Content>Wonderful place The moment you enter the hotel you have the most amazing view in front of you. This is one of the best things with Ritz-Carlton, Bali. In conclusion, a very nice place.

<Content>Did Not Meet Expectations My wife and I stayed a single night out of a planned five nights.What we liked were the immaculate grounds, spacious and beautiful. Palm trees, flowers, and well attended landscaping. We liked the room itself, very clean, upgraded bedding, large bathroom and lots of marble. We had booked a 'deluxe ocean view'.What we did not like was the marble floors that clicked clacked with each step of the guests above us, well into the night. The 'ocean view' is some far off stretch of blue several hundred yards from our room. The breakfast buffet was ordinary, not bad, but Holiday Inn level. You had better like laying around the pool, because the strip of sand that substitues for a beach lies 5 flights of stairs up and down the cliff to reach it. The 'beach' also has a bad habit of being completely submerged at high tide.The cliffside villas would be a more pleasurable experience but are pricey plus 21% service charge and tax.We left after the first night and went to the Sheraton Laguna @ Nusa Dua. That was less expensive, had a real beach, and more fun as we could jump into the lagoon right from our room level deck.

<Content>disappointed We stayed here in June and like others thought we were pampering ourselves during the first 5 days of our two week honeymoon. Our experience at the buffet breakfast every morning was that they weren't too fond of westerners. I will say the food at the breakfast was amazing if you are adventurous with asian cuisine.There are so many beautiful villas in Bali with more of less the same service that you will find at the Ritz for the same price our less. I would have never stayed at the Ritz or any hotel had I known that I could have a private pool in an enclosed villa in Nusa or Seminyak for the same price or less - including at 24x7 butler.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Ritz Carlton Bali - Not Impressed! My wife and I just returned home (New York) from Bali (June 12th 2005) and we found the Ritz Carlton to be overrated and disappointing.We wanted a luxurious getaway but the Ritz Carlton was quite lacking. We ended up switching to the Four Seasons at Jimbaran Bay and that was the only salvation in our trip.We arrived at the RC around 2 in the afternoon and were told we would have to wait for check in. Ok, that is fine but we ended up sitting in the uncomfortable lobby and nobody even asked if they wanted us to hold our baggage. We eventually were permitted to check in at 5:00 in the evening and found the villa we reserved to be oddly American-appearing. There was nothing Balinese about it. It almost reminded me of the suite we stayed in at the Ritz in Palm Beach except a few more statues.The private pool was a disaster as it had mold and bugs everywhere. We immediately contacted the manager and asked to be switched to another villa. Luckily that was possible since they were only near 25% occupancy. So, we swithced to another villa which at least had an appropriate pool. The villa itself was quite smaller than I expected. In addition, the view was only average considering my expectations.By the next morning, we went for breakfast after being woken up by loud noises around 7 in the morning. Not a good way to start the day. There must have been some corporate meeting going on because the restaurant was full of obvious aspiring business hopefuls. I thought we would have it peaceful, but no such luck as they all seem to fight over who can speak the loudest.We tried to spend the day relaxing on the grounds, but, again, the grounds are basically like anything you would see in the US. I might has well have taken a nonstop flight to Key Biscayne and avoided the whole problem.Anyway, after retiring to our relatively small and uncomofrtable villa that evening, we discussed our options. We called the Four Seasons and luckily they had two villas left for the balance of the week. They came and picked us up before breakfast the next morning, treated us to a spectaculr complimentary breafast before checking us in at 10:00 AM. There was no comparison between the two villas. The Four Seasons made you feel you were truly in Bali. The villa at the FS was much cleaner, spacious, airy, and simply relaxing.Thank you, Four Seasons for making our vacation to Bali what it needed to be.Ritz, please work on improving things.

<Author>Ricksy999
<Content>Wow. We loved the Ritzzzzzzz!!! Hi. We have read all grumbles about the Ritz and after staying there for 9 days for our honeymoon can honestly say... What planet are these people on!!!!!!. This resort is absolutely stunning. Its perfect for anyone wanting privacy, luxury and pure indulgence in the most breathtaking setting. The club rooms seemed to get the bad press the most and we cant comment as we stayed in the main hotel (2 nights) and then upgraded to a cliff villa (7 nights). The hotel rooms are clean, modern and efficiently cleaned by the resorts mega friendly staff. However its the cliff villas that are the most spectacular thing about the ritz. We upgraded for a mere $500 and spent a whole week living like kings. The villas are only 6 months old (approx) and are set on the cliff overlooking the Indian Ocean. You enter through your traditional balinese carved doors with a massive gong for a doorbell. The lounge is tastefully furnished and well equipped with all modern gadgets. The bedroom has a romantic four poster bed with drapes and leads through to the biggest bathroom we have ever seen. Like a roman bath. Stunning. However, the most attrctive feature of the villa has got to be the private plunge pool!!. Nothing like watching the sun set over the Indian Ocean in your own swimming pool with a glass of champagne served by your personal butler!!!If you even need to leave these amazing villas (are you mad) then summon your butler who will whisk you anywhere around the resort in a golf buggy. Now to the resort in general....Grounds... Well kept and maintained with great balance of water features, polished marble, vegetation and statues all surrounding some lovely ponds with lillies and Koi carp.Swimming Pools....Giant main swimming pool situated at the bottom of the resort over looking the cliff. Staff bend overbackwards to help you and provide ice cream, fruit, water and cold towels throughout the day free of charge. Cliff Villa Swimming pools.....Even more funky and luxurious pools for use of cliff villa guests only.Restaurants.....Four or five excellent restaurants. Would recommend Sami Sami for breakfast (less busy and fewer Japanese and has excellent views over the ocean). Note the restaurants are not cheap for Bali prices but hey this is the Ritz!!!! and you only get what you pay for. For honeymooner's we recommend the Kisik restaurant at the bottom of the cliff. Bit of a trek and harder coming up but worth the effort for the romantic sunset. Spa..... looked fabulous but had a great massage in Bel Air Spa Jimbaran for 1/3 of the price. Beach......Kubu beach is the Ritz-Carlton's private beach. We agree that the 150 odd steps are a pain, especially coming back up but the beach is well worth the effort. Clean, scenic and isolated it is totally relaxing and If you time it right you can be the only ones on it!. Staff are also on hand to serve food, drinks and those cold towels. Unlike other Bali beaches, there are no hawkers which you really appreciate.Staff..... No complaints what so ever. Very friendly and helpful. I ordered a cheese burger by room service and the chef phoned up to send his profound apologies that Camambert wasn't available and would I settle for cheddar to go with my burger. Well funny!!!All in all the Ritz is an amazing hotel and perfect for honeymooners or anyone wanting pure indulgence and luxury. The location is stunning and close enough for a short taxi ride to the amazing Jimbaran Beach for a Warung seafood feast. We visited the four seasons Jimbaran and Sayan and we think the Ritz has the edge over facilities and prices. Remember make sure you get a Cliff Villa. WOOOOW.!!!

<Author>escholte
<Content>Thoroughly enjoyable stay We had a great stay in March at the Ritz-Carlton at Jimbaran Bay. We stayed in a club level suite and had the unfortunate accident of a burst water pipe over the closet. The management were quick to respond giving us an alternative suite for the night and arranged to have any wet clothes laundered. The next day we were offered a villa with pool as apology and a bit of further bargaining got us a well placed villa so that we could still enjoy the Club facilties. The food presentations were good - why do a lot of people thinks it's their meal for the day. The villa was lovely but we would have preferred the suite with a better view. The pools were lovely, the setting nice except little allowance for disabled customers - too many steps. They even baked a birthday cake for my partner for free and the club team even gave him a present. The hotel has a strong Japanese client base. Also the CLub as mentioned by others has mostly tables and chairs with little relaxing space.The downside was: far from Kuta but at 拢3 for a 20 minute taxi trip - it is not going to break the bank. The +++ can be soul destroying at times as the restaurants were not value for money.On balance an enjoyable stay but might think of the Oberoi next time as closer to restaurants, night life, etc.

<Author>Natonhols
<Content>Disappointing 20-22 March, 2005Set in a magnificent location overlooking the ocean - the view is amazing. That was the only impressive part of our stay though.We booked 2 nights at the Ritz-Carlton in Jimbaran Bay, thinking it'd a little taste of luxury in comparison to the other resorts in which we were spending the rest of our time in Bali. We were disappointed from the moment we arrived at our room. We were given a room with an inter-connecting door to the room next door - which we had not requested. These doors provide very little sound proofing between rooms, something which was proved to us within 2 minutes of arriving in the room by hearing very clearly the activities that were going on in the room next to us. We immediately requested a change of room - a request that was initially denied, but after a 2 hour wait, we were eventually moved to another room at 7.30pm (which meant we missed our first Jimbaran sunset). Unfortunately, even though this room did not have an inter-connecting door, there still wasn't much sound proofing between rooms. We could hear the occupants on either side of us quite clearly, and were woken each morning by the thumping of the people above us getting up each morning, then kept awake by the noise of people walking past our room down the tiled hallway - really quite loud. The hotel, which is located a 20+ minute drive from Kuta, doesn't offer a suitable shuttle service. Four shuttles per day, with 10 people per shuttle (ie. 5 couples), with the shuttle being required to be booked 24 hours in advance. This is totally inadequate for a hotel with over 375 rooms! It seems a good way for the hotel - which charges extortionate US$ for everything (IRP300,000 for Nasi Gorang which costs about IRP35,000 in a restaurant) - to keep guests at the hotel where they can spend their tourist dollars. That being said, metered taxis (only) are on call from the foyer.We found the staff to be helpful at a minimal level - the hotel had a 92% occupancy rate when we were there so it seemed that they really didn't care if we had a problem. Such a dramatic difference to the other hotels/restorts we stayed in where staff couldn't be more helpful. Housekeeping didn't arrive until 3pm (rooms are attended to between 7.30am and 4.30pm), which meant no clean towels, no bottled drinking water etc until late in the day. For such a large, well known hotel, it just seemed to be really lacking in service. The breakfast buffet is good, but even though the buffet goes until 10.30am, get there early, because once the food runs out it isn't always replaced. I was there at 9.30am and most of the hot western buffet was gone (there is also a Japanese buffet - the hotel was mainly full of Japanese tourists - I'd say about 85%+). We found it hard to find staff for a coffee top-up or glass of water. So much for our luxurious, relaxing time at the Ritz-Carlton. I won't be returning and certainly wouldn't recommend it to my friends. We found the smaller Legian Hotel in Seminyak to be so much better - larger rooms for less money, fantastic, friendly, professional staff, great guest services, cool face towels and ice cold water provided at the pool, sensational food and much closer to shopping  terrific restaurants!!  
<Date>Mar 29, 2005
